It seems you are referring to a concept related to the bones of the fetal skeleton, which can be described as follows: The fetal skeleton starts off with more flexible and cartilaginous structures rather than fully-formed bone tissue found in adults. As development progresses, these cartilages gradually ossify through a process known as endochondral ossification, where the cartilage is replaced by bone tissue. This transition starts around the 8th week of gestation and continues until about age 25 when most of the growth plates (epiphyseal plates) have fully ossified into epiphyses. Additionally, there are also important transitions such as the fusion of cranial sutures that occurs postnatally to complete the skull formation.
